  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p> The Presto SQL Parser was perfect for phase one of the SQLHandler. It was nicely split off from the larger Presto project and it did everything that was needed for the initial implementation.</p> 
                  <p>Phase two of the SQL work though will require an optimizer. Here is where Apache Calcite comes into play. It has a battle tested cost based optimizer and has been integrated into Apache Drill and Hive.</p> 
                  <p>This work can begin in trunk following the 6.0 release. The final query plans will continue to be translated to Streaming API objects (TupleStreams), so continued work on the JDBC driver should plug in nicely with the Calcite work.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

\u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15204891_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'21\\/Mar\\/16 18:52\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-03-21T18:52:58+0000\'\u003e21\\/Mar\\/16 18:52\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003e\u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=joel.bernstein\\\" class=\\\"user-hover\\\" rel=\\\"joel.bernstein\\\"\u003eJoel Bernstein\u003c\\/a\u003e - I took a much closer look at Calcite and the \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/SOLR-7560\\\" title=\\\"Parallel SQL Support\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"SOLR-7560\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eSOLR-7560\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e patch. I think there can be a much simpler approach than implementing the parsing and catalog separately. If a Calcite adaptor is built that enables Calcite to access Solr this would solve a lot of problems at once potentially. Calcite has a local JDBC connection which you can just pass in a SQL query and get back a result set. This local JDBC connection could be wrapped in a stream and returned from the \\/sql handler. This would remove the need for the limit\\/having\\/etc streams that currently exist. The logic for pushing down having\\/limit\\/etc would have to be moved into how Calcite does the processing. This should make the SQL handler much simpler since it would pass off much of the work its doing to Calcite. The downside to this approach is that much of the logic would be Calcite specific and need to figure out exactly which hooks to tie into.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"risdenk\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_15204891_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=risdenk\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"risdenk\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Kevin Risden\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15204891_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'21\\/Mar\\/16 18:52\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-03-21T18:52:58+0000\'\u003e21\\/Mar\\/16 18:52\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                     Joel Bernstein  - I took a much closer look at Calcite and the   SOLR-7560   patch. I think there can be a much simpler approach than implementing the parsing and catalog separately. If a Calcite adaptor is built that enables Calcite to access Solr this would solve a lot of problems at once potentially. Calcite has a local JDBC connection which you can just pass in a SQL query and get back a result set. This local JDBC connection could be wrapped in a stream and returned from the \\/sql handler. This would remove the need for the limit\\/having\\/etc streams that currently exist. The logic for pushing down having\\/limit\\/etc would have to be moved into how Calcite does the processing. This should make the SQL handler much simpler since it would pass off much of the work its doing to Calcite. The downside to this approach is that much of the logic would be Calcite specific and need to figure out exactly which hooks to tie into.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/SOLR-8593?focusedCommentId=15376266&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-15376266\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=julianhyde\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"julianhyde\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Julian Hyde\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15376266_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'14\\/Jul\\/16 03:42\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-07-14T03:42:21+0000\'\u003e14\\/Jul\\/16 03:42\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eYou should probably model your join and aggregate operators as sub-classes of Join and Aggregate that understand the \\\"distribution\\\" trait. If you are doing, say, \\\"group by x\\\" then you will need your input either to be singleton (i.e. only one input stream) or partitioned on x. Calcite will be able to ensure that the input is partitioned appropriately, either because it is stored in partitions, or by applying a shuffle\\/exchange. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThere is the regular Exchange operator that changes the distribution (i.e. re-partitions) and there is SortExchange that changes the distribution and also sorts within each partition. SortExchange models what the shuffle does in MapReduce.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAfter you have a plan like\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"preformatted panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"preformattedContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre\u003eMyJoin[left.a = right.b]\\n  Exchange[a]\\n    MyAggregate\\n      Exchange\\n        Scan[T1]\\n  Exchange[b]\\n    Scan[T2]\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eyou can turn into map-reduce by making the consumer of each Exchange into a reduce task, and the input to each Exchange a map task.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI asked \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=ashutoshc\\\" class=\\\"user-hover\\\" rel=\\\"ashutoshc\\\"\u003eAshutosh Chauhan\u003c\\/a\u003e how he would generate Hive MapReduce plans in Calcite (most Hive plans these days are Tez) and he said you should consider writing a CoGroup operator (like the one in Pig). CoGroup is powerful enough to implement both join and aggregate, so it might save you some effort.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"julianhyde\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_15376266_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=julianhyde\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"julianhyde\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Julian Hyde\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15376266_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'14\\/Jul\\/16 03:42\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-07-14T03:42:21+0000\'\u003e14\\/Jul\\/16 03:42\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    You should probably model your join and aggregate operators as sub-classes of Join and Aggregate that understand the \\\"distribution\\\" trait. If you are doing, say, \\\"group by x\\\" then you will need your input either to be singleton (i.e. only one input stream) or partitioned on x. Calcite will be able to ensure that the input is partitioned appropriately, either because it is stored in partitions, or by applying a shuffle\\/exchange.  \\n\\n There is the regular Exchange operator that changes the distribution (i.e. re-partitions) and there is SortExchange that changes the distribution and also sorts within each partition. SortExchange models what the shuffle does in MapReduce. \\n\\n After you have a plan like \\n\\n  \\n MyJoin[left.a = right.b]\\n  Exchange[a]\\n    MyAggregate\\n      Exchange\\n        Scan[T1]\\n  Exchange[b]\\n    Scan[T2]\\n \\n  \\n\\n you can turn into map-reduce by making the consumer of each Exchange into a reduce task, and the input to each Exchange a map task. \\n\\n I asked  Ashutosh Chauhan  how he would generate Hive MapReduce plans in Calcite (most Hive plans these days are Tez) and he said you should consider writing a CoGroup operator (like the one in Pig). CoGroup is powerful enough to implement both join and aggregate, so it might save you some effort.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eOne thing that you may have to do to make the Solr server happy until Calcite 1.11 gets released is put the solr-core jar in front of calcite-core on the classpath. They are alphabetical right now (I fixed by renaming solr-core to asolr-core). This is to make sure the CalciteConnectionProperty fixes goes in before the original version. Otherwise you get an abstract method error.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eselect count(distinct) ... might actually work right now with that patch. If it doesn\'t then comment out the rules in the static block in SolrRules. That should give the full power of just regular SQL on top of Solr. It wouldn\'t really push anything down but still the SQL works. (This should include joins)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eYou should be able to add\\/change the SolrRules to see what gets pushed down. Otherwise you get an abstract method error. \\n\\n select count(distinct) ... might actually work right now with that patch. If it doesn\'t then comment out the rules in the static block in SolrRules. That should give the full power of just regular SQL on top of Solr. It wouldn\'t really push anything down but still the SQL works. (This should include joins) \\n\\n You should be able to add\\/change the SolrRules to see what gets pushed down. The classes from the branch are the exact same as the code here:  https:\\/\\/github.com\\/risdenk\\/solr-calcite-example  The code there has some more tests that show the explain plan. flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eRegarding the alias for \\\"count(&#42;)\\\". I guess one approach is to extend Calcite to allow a pluggable alias derivation (it has to be pluggable because you can\'t please everyone). Another approach is to leave the aliases as they are but generate field names for the JSON result set. Note that if you call SqlNode.getParserPosition() on each item in the select clause it will tell you the start and end point of that expression in the original SQL string, so you can extract the \\\"count(&#42;)\\\" using that information.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI don\'t think the the following should be valid, but under your proposed change it would be:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003eSELECT deptno\\nFROM (\\n  SELECT deptno, count(*)\\n  FROM emp\\n  GROUP BY deptno) AS t\\nWHERE t.\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"count(*)\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e &gt; 3\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eNote that \\\"count(&#42;)\\\" is not an expression; it is a reference to a \\\"column\\\" produced by the sub-query. In my opinion, using a textual expression is very confusing, and we should not do it. Derived alias of \u003ctt\u003ecount(&#42;)\u003c\\/tt\u003e should be something not easily guessable, which will encourage users to use an alias:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003eSELECT deptno\\nFROM (\\n  SELECT deptno, count(*) AS c\\n  FROM emp\\n  GROUP BY deptno) AS t\\nWHERE t.c &gt; 3\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"julianhyde\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_15664576_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=julianhyde\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"julianhyde\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Julian Hyde\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15664576_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'14\\/Nov\\/16 18:10\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-11-14T18:10:48+0000\'\u003e14\\/Nov\\/16 18:10\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Julian Hyde - 14\\/Nov\\/16 18:11\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   Regarding the alias for \\\"count(&#42;)\\\". I guess one approach is to extend Calcite to allow a pluggable alias derivation (it has to be pluggable because you can\'t please everyone). Another approach is to leave the aliases as they are but generate field names for the JSON result set. Note that if you call SqlNode.getParserPosition() on each item in the select clause it will tell you the start and end point of that expression in the original SQL string, so you can extract the \\\"count(&#42;)\\\" using that information. \\n\\n I don\'t think the the following should be valid, but under your proposed change it would be: \\n\\n  \\n SELECT deptno\\nFROM (\\n  SELECT deptno, count(*)\\n  FROM emp\\n  GROUP BY deptno) AS t\\nWHERE t. \\\"count(*)\\\"  &gt; 3\\n \\n  \\n\\n Note that \\\"count(&#42;)\\\" is not an expression; it is a reference to a \\\"column\\\" produced by the sub-query. In my opinion, using a textual expression is very confusing, and we should not do it. Derived alias of  count(&#42;)  should be something not easily guessable, which will encourage users to use an alias: \\n\\n  \\n SELECT deptno\\nFROM (\\n  SELECT deptno, count(*) AS c\\n  FROM emp\\n  GROUP BY deptno) AS t\\nWHERE t.c &gt; 3\\n \\n               \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Joel Bernstein - 05\\/Dec\\/16 16:17\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   I wanted to give an update on my work on this ticket. \\n\\n I\'ve started working my way through the test cases (TestSQLHandler). I\'m working through each assertion in each method to understand the differences between the current release and the work done in this patch, and making changes\\/fixes as I go. \\n\\n The first change that I made was in how the predicate is being traversed. The current patch doesn\'t descend through a full nested AND\\/OR predicate. So I made a few changes to how the tree is walked. I also changed some of the logic for how the query is re-written to a Lucene\\/Solr query so that it matches the current implementation. \\n\\n I\'ve now moved on to aggregate queries. I\'ve been investigating the use of EXPR$1 ... instead of using the  function signature  in the result set. It looks like we\'ll have to use the Caclite expression identifiers going forward, which should be OK. I think this is cleaner anyway because looking up fields by a function signature can get cumbersome. We\'ll just need to document this in the CHANGES.txt. \\n\\n The next step for me is to implement the aggregationMode=facet logic for aggregate queries. After that I\'ll push out my changes to this branch.  \\n\\n Then I\'ll spend some time investigating how SELECT DISTINCT behaves with our Calcite implementation. As  Julian Hyde  mentioned, we should see DISTINCT queries as aggregate queries so it\'s possible we\'ll have all the code in place to push this to Solr already. \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf you we have two grouping fields \u003cb\u003eA, B\u003c\\/b\u003e nested facets will be gathered using the following \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15753373_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'16\\/Dec\\/16 04:09\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-12-16T04:09:54+0000\'\u003e16\\/Dec\\/16 04:09\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    If you we have two grouping fields  A, B  nested facets will be gathered using the following approach: \\n\\n 1) Gather the  top N  facets for field A. \\n2) For each of the   top N  facets of field A, find the top N sub-facets for field B \\n\\n This avoids the exhaustive processing of all the unique combinations of A, B. \\n\\n This is very performant (sub-second) when N is a relatively small number and the cardinality of A, B is not too high. \\n\\n In high cardinality scenarios we can switch to MapReduce mode which sorts the Tuples on the GROUP BY fields and shuffles them to worker nodes. In MapReduce mode the order of the GROUP BY fields is not important. \\n\\n Having the ability to use faceting or MapReduce depending on cardinality is one of the key features of Solr\'s SQL implementation.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-15753387\\\" flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eNot sure I understand. The query \u003ctt\u003eselect a from b limit 10\u003c\\/tt\u003e will have a \u003ctt\u003eSort\u003c\\/tt\u003e whose key has zero fields but which has fetch = 10. The \u003ctt\u003eSort\u003c\\/tt\u003e will be translated to a \u003ctt\u003eSolrSort\u003c\\/tt\u003e with similar attributes. The sort is trivial - that is, you don\'t need to do any work to sort on 0 fields - but you do need to apply the limit. If you see a \u003ctt\u003eSolrSort\u003c\\/tt\u003e with empty keys, don\'t drop it, but maybe convert into a \u003ctt\u003eSolrLimit\u003c\\/tt\u003e if you have such a thing.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eYou may be wondering why we combine sort and limit into the same operator. But remember that relational data sets are inherently unordered, so we have to do them at the same time. Sort with an empty key has reasonable semantics, just as &#8211; I hope you agree &#8211; Aggregate with an empty key (e.g. \u003ctt\u003eselect count&#40;&#42;&#41; from emp\u003c\\/tt\u003e, which is equivalent to \u003ctt\u003eselect count&#40;&#42;&#41; from emp group by ()\u003c\\/tt\u003e) is a reasonable generalization of Aggregate.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"julianhyde\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_15849145_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=julianhyde\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"julianhyde\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Julian Hyde\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15849145_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Feb\\/17 00:04\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2017-02-02T00:04:34+0000\'\u003e02\\/Feb\\/17 00:04\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Julian Hyde - 02\\/Feb\\/17 00:05\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   Not sure I understand. The query  select a from b limit 10  will have a  Sort  whose key has zero fields but which has fetch = 10. The  Sort  will be translated to a  SolrSort  with similar attributes. The sort is trivial - that is, you don\'t need to do any work to sort on 0 fields - but you do need to apply the limit. If you see a  SolrSort  with empty keys, don\'t drop it, but maybe convert into a  SolrLimit  if you have such a thing. \\n\\n You may be wondering why we combine sort and limit into the same operator. Sort with an empty key has reasonable semantics, just as &#8211; I hope you agree &#8211; Aggregate with an empty key (e.g.  select count&#40;&#42;&#41; from emp , which is equivalent to  select
